  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b7de74d6-7d32-4287-8f84-3e9d531b35d5'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText8362832184472392790" style="display:none">When Adam Blake lands the best elective ever in his senior year, serving as an aide to the school psychologist, he thinks he’s got it made. Sure, it means a lot of sitting around, which isn’t easy for a guy with ADHD, but he can’t complain, since he gets to spend the period texting all his friends. Then the doctor asks him to track down the troubled freshman who keeps dodging her, and Adam discovers that the boy is Julian—the foster brother he hasn’t seen in five years.<br /><br />Adam is ecstatic to be reunited. At first, Julian seems like the boy he once knew. He’s still kindhearted. He still writes stories and loves picture books meant for little kids. But as they spend more time together, Adam realizes that Julian is keeping secrets, like where he hides during the middle of the day, and what’s really going on inside his house. Adam is determined to help him, but his involvement could cost both boys their lives…</span>

<div id="review_1977374067" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1977374067" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1977374067?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1977374067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12514002154748538337">I don’t know how a book can splinter in my mind with a haze of pain around it, make tears spring unbidden to my eyes and generally feel as though I was seeing into a bottomless well of anguish, but then, right when I thought the flint shell of my heart would crack, it hits me with a keen pang of hope and sets like a little ball of tingling warmth in the pit of my stomach.<br/><br/><em>A List of Cages</em> is a beautiful, soul-crushing love letter to friendships that heal the broken pathways of your heart and hope </span>
  <span id="freeText12514002154748538337" style="display:none">I don’t know how a book can splinter in my mind with a haze of pain around it, make tears spring unbidden to my eyes and generally feel as though I was seeing into a bottomless well of anguish, but then, right when I thought the flint shell of my heart would crack, it hits me with a keen pang of hope and sets like a little ball of tingling warmth in the pit of my stomach.<br /><br /><em>A List of Cages</em> is a beautiful, soul-crushing love letter to friendships that heal the broken pathways of your heart and hope that can’t be washed away by the torrent of despair, to the pain we survive in youth and to the courage it takes to will your fragments into finding a way to mesh back together into a single person. <strong>It’s a reminder that we are better than the worst things that we’ve been made to endure.</strong> But mostly, this book was a sigh of relief at the knowledge that kindness can exist in this world, and the mournful remorse of kindness existing in a world that doesn’t really deserve it.<br /><br />After the death of his parents in a tragic accident, Julian Harlow’s life had smashed and spilled him tumbling away from the loving foster home of Adam Blake and his mother into the brutal guardianship of his uncle. Five years later, Adam—a senior—is assigned the duty of escorting a freshman to the counseling sessions he persists in skipping. The freshman is none other than his former foster brother, Julian. <br /><br />Adam is thrilled to be reunited with his friend, but the years have remade Julian into a shadow version of himself and no matter how much Adam tried to root through what was hidden in the labyrinth of Julian’s memories, his burden was to feel all the pain of Julian’s unspoken torment, and not know how to help him. But while Adam was thinking of Julian’s bruises and frequent absences and his uncle’s house that conjured no feeling of “home”, another thought tiptoed between them. It was sly, odious and unnameable, and it waited to be noticed...<br /><br />In this book, we see the vast extent of damage <strong>abuse</strong>—both physical and emotional—inflicts on survivors. How weary one’s chest becomes from carrying all the repeated hope and disappointment and how so used they become to every-day life being painful that they begin to doubt any path that doesn’t come with agony. We see how abusers learn to masquerade as things that wouldn’t seem threatening to get close enough to strike and how oftentimes they’re the same people who are supposed to protect you from the ravages of the world but instead wrap their manipulations in the chain of the security and sense of self-worth which they claim to offer you.<br /><br />But nothing broke my heart more than how quick everyone—his classmates, his teachers, his principle—was to fill Julian’s silences with their own interpretation: He was depressed. He was awkward. He was weird. He was stuck up. He was judgmental. They couldn’t read him so they wrote their own story, and they didn’t care enough to see into the pain that traced along each one of his unspoken scars. They were all continuously watching this massive, looming thing over Julian’s life to which they were supposed to promptly apply the adjective <em>dangerous</em> and <strong>immediately act</strong>. But they didn’t—not until it was too late anyway. And the fact that <em>Robin Roe</em> herself is a counselor and a mentor for at-risk teenagers who must have encountered many cases like this in real life still nudges at the dark of my thoughts.<br /><br /><em>A List of Cages</em> was heart-breakingly hard to read, yes, but I’m grateful for the bedrock of love and affection that was always there, because the real story, ultimately, is in the relationships. This is a book that drips with love and approaches its characters with a whole-hearted delight in their differences, similarities, and connections—Adam’s utter, unflinching aura of love that was all around him and Julian’s jangling, nerve-racking, mind-screaming strength. <br /><br /><strong>Julian and Adam’s friendship made me cry.</strong> That friendship was the moon, the gentle glow that illuminated the darkness around Julian. It made it easier to see the path stretching before him, and Julian stumbled less in its light, and found himself looking up at it in awe. It’s that friendship and it's that kindness that eventually uncovers the border between hope and despair that had become lost in the fear.<br /><br />I think the greatest takeaway from this book is that maybe there’s not much any of us can do: you’re small and weak and helpless and you can be so clumsy with words when words mean so much. But you know you can be kind. And sometimes, I believe, that changes the world. Or just someone's world. So please, <em>please</em>, if anything, just be kind.<br /><br /><b>TRIGGER WARNINGS:</b> violence, emotional and physical abuse.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12514002154748538337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2340238891" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2340238891" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2340238891?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2340238891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer898365995129399066">If this story doesn’t make you emotional, I have to bring to the table the idea that you might actually be an android. Yes, you've been exposed. <br/><br/>Because how could anyone be unaffected by such injustice and cruelty toward a fourteen-year-old?<br/><br/>Julian’s parents died when he was a child, leaving him with a foster care family for some time, and then with his uncle Russell, who has been abusing him both mentally and physically since.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, like other victims of abuse, Julian doesn’t understand </span>
  <span id="freeText898365995129399066" style="display:none">If this story doesn’t make you emotional, I have to bring to the table the idea that you might actually be an android. Yes, you've been exposed. <br /><br />Because how could anyone be unaffected by such injustice and cruelty toward a fourteen-year-old?<br /><br />Julian’s parents died when he was a child, leaving him with a foster care family for some time, and then with his uncle Russell, who has been abusing him both mentally and physically since.<br /><br />Unfortunately, like other victims of abuse, Julian doesn’t understand that what he’s experiencing at home is not normal, so he doesn’t know he needs help. Though his friendship with Adam does make him question some of his uncle’s actions and ways of thinking, such as why he insists on Julian shaving his legs. <br /><br />Julian and Adam may be four years apart in age, but that doesn’t keep them from being able to connect to one another on a meaningful level – so meaningful that it made me realize that friendships between two young men are rarely so thoroughly explored in YA contemporary, without going in the romantic direction. <br /><br />It’s beautifully-touching and never manipulative. The author doesn’t seek to control our reactions, but of course being the decent human beings that we are, we quickly notice that Russell has deep-rooted issues that only hurt Julian and prevent him from living a good life. <br /><br />I can’t believe it took me so long to give this one a chance, especially since I read it in a single day. I was afraid it would be too dark, but while Robin Roe does include scenes that are hard to witness, her goal isn’t to overwhelm us to the point of not being able to read this book either. <br /><br />An excellent debut novel. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="898365995129399066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=disability">disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1798525122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4769617127382780415"><b>This is the most precious cinnamon roll of a book I have ever read.</b> It absolutely DAMAGED MY SOUL but it was beautiful and heartfelt and the characters just sort of sneaked off the page and became incredibly real and relatable people to me and just GAHHHHH I LOVED IT SO MUCH I CANNOT EVEN. <br/><br/>(Also this is my first 5 star read of the year!! I'm so excited!!)<br/><br/><b>Basically this is a story about friendship and abuse.</b> I will warn you: it's not easy to read. It does heavily feature child abuse and stockholm</span>
  <span id="freeText4769617127382780415" style="display:none"><b>This is the most precious cinnamon roll of a book I have ever read.</b> It absolutely DAMAGED MY SOUL but it was beautiful and heartfelt and the characters just sort of sneaked off the page and became incredibly real and relatable people to me and just GAHHHHH I LOVED IT SO MUCH I CANNOT EVEN. <br /><br />(Also this is my first 5 star read of the year!! I'm so excited!!)<br /><br /><b>Basically this is a story about friendship and abuse.</b> I will warn you: it's not easy to read. It does heavily feature child abuse and stockholm syndrome and psychological torture. IT'S REALLY BITTERLY HEARTBREAKING. I'm like the Vulcan of the century so I didn't <i>cry</i>, but I was definitely in a tangled knot on the inside.<br /><br /><b>And I so loved the emphasis on friendship.</b> Also how it was "unconventional" friendship. It's dual narrated by <b>Adam and Julian</b>. They met when they were little because Julian has dyslexia and Adam was in a group helping younger kids to read. There's actually <b>a four year age gap</b> between them AND I LOVED THIS. Not only did it show us that <b>(A)</b> it is awesome and great to be friends with people who aren't necessarily your same age, and <b>(B) </b>it had a really big-brother-little-brother feel to the friendship too. (And brotherly stories are actually my favourite thing.)<br /><br /><b>And the characters?! THEY WERE RIDICULOUSLY PRECIOUS.</b> Even though they both narrated in 1st person, I felt their voices were super different! Adam's chapters were more bouncy and bright, while Julian's were timid and cautious. <b>And the fact that I could SEE that in the writing is just afjdksalfd incredibly talented word wizarding.</b><br /><br /><b>ADAM:</b> he has ADHD and is in his senior year at highschool. He is 100% Mr. Happy and like how incredibly refreshing was it to read about a happy boy?!? I LOVED IT. And he cares fiercely about people, although he's often obviously to subtleties. Which is very realistic for ADHD people, as far as I know.<br /><b>JULIAN:</b> he has dyslexia and he's just started higschool (I think?)...he's 14 anyway. IDK HOW YOUR AMERICAN HIGHSCHOOLS WORK. Anyway. His parents died when he was little so he went from a goofy little kid to this timid shy depressed child...and it just got worse when his abusive uncle adopted him. The abuse Julian goes through is horrifying to read and crushing and, gah, I just wanted to snatch him out of this book and keep him safe. But watching him rekindle his friendship with Adam and learn he's wanted and worthwhile was absolutely amazing.<br /><br /><b>I also am so pleased it featured boys with disabilities.</b> Disabilities is something I don't often get to see a lot of in books! SO YAY FOR REP. And it also didn't gloss over what it's like to have your life impacted by a disability (particularly a sort of "invisible" disability like these where a lot of people don't believe you have it or choose to ignore/erase it). <b>They're actually treated REALLY HORRIBLY by most people around them, though.</b> So <i>that</i> was hard to read. Their teachers have 0% caring for disabilities. Julian's dyslexia is "his fault". No one's helping him and he's failing school because he can't read/write well enough. Adam gets in trouble for his ADHD a lot, but at least he has a supportive mother.<br /><br /><b>Ohhhh and you know something else that impressed me?! It talked about how medication isn't the ONLY way to deal with things!</b> It's not anti-medication, don't worry. But you know what? Medication doesn't work for everybody. And I just kind of flailed when Adam and his mum were using good diets and homeopathic remedies to help manage his ADHD. It was really relatable to me because this is what my family does. &lt;3 So just thank you to the author, THANK YOU SO MUCH, for representing natural alternatives and not sneering on them. (They don't always work either, okay, but neither does medication. And it's so nice to see balance.)<br /><br /><b>I'M JUST SITTING HERE FLAILING ETERNALLY. I HOPE YOU ALL DON'T MIND</b>.<br /><br /><b>Also the book is really small, so I just flew through it!</b> I think sometimes the smallness worked against it, a bit, because there were things that were glossed over. I still have questions and a few things confused me <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like how, after Julian was released from hospital to Adam's family after nearly being murdered by his uncle, how he didn't have to go to a psych or anything? I can't imagine that they'd have not required him to get counselling after a near death experience. Plus it didn't really talk more about his eating disorder. I figured he wasn't eating in the hospital because as long as he STAYED in the hospital, he was "safe"...but then when he found out he'd go home with Adam, he tried harder. But I do wish it'd discussed if the eating disorder stayed or what Julian's thought process about it was. Things like that. He just would've had so many mental health issues and yet he was allowed to just not do anything about them. ALSO I don't know what he was doing about school. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>AND IT KIND OF SOCKED ME IN THE FEELS.</b> Which I love and appreciate. How are these characters just so incredibly precious?!? They were so different and yet so wonderful and I GUSH. And like when Adam + his senior friends decided to "adopt" Julian during school hours and just take care of him??? Be still my beating heart.<br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: look you need this book in your life.</b> I'm hugging it with affection and I loved the boys and I loved how it represented disabilities. It wasn't a fair book. It wasn't an easy book. It wasn't always a kind book. But <b>I think it was realistic and it definitely made me think</b>. And I love love looooooove books that focus on friendship. <b>FRIENDSHIP IS IMPORTANT AND KNOWS NO BOUNDS.</b> <br /><br />PS. Go read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4769617127382780415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer8688549678077746236">every once in awhile i am truly blown away by a story. i will read something that exceeds all of my expectations and more. the book will cause me feel a range of emotions that i didnt expect to experience. its a story that burrows itself deep into my heart. it doesnt happen often, but when it does, im left astounded. like i am this very moment.<br/><br/>this was very heavy for a YA contemporary novel, but i am so thankful for that. it shows that really tough things happen to young people. it shows that ev</span>
  <span id="freeText8688549678077746236" style="display:none">every once in awhile i am truly blown away by a story. i will read something that exceeds all of my expectations and more. the book will cause me feel a range of emotions that i didnt expect to experience. its a story that burrows itself deep into my heart. it doesnt happen often, but when it does, im left astounded. like i am this very moment.<br /><br />this was very heavy for a YA contemporary novel, but i am so thankful for that. it shows that really tough things happen to young people. it shows that every person is able to make a difference. it shows that even the most difficult of times can lead to something better. i love this book for showing that. its a heartbreaking story, but it is also a story beautiful story of love and hope. <br /><br />this is the kind of book that leaves the reader better than it found it, and for that, i am truly grateful and humbled. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2396520129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2396520129" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2396520129?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2396520129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12707175941376064898"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I know what I think, but people don't want you to say what you think. They want you to say what they think. And knowing what that is isn't easy.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Mental health books are some of my favorites to read because they're so powerful and beautiful, capturing you in the struggled lives of the people suffering and living with this illness they have. Every book I've read that is labeled as a "contemporary mental health book" has been one I've loved, like and enjoyed. I haven't ended up disliking</span>
  <span id="freeText12707175941376064898" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I know what I think, but people don't want you to say what you think. They want you to say what they think. And knowing what that is isn't easy.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Mental health books are some of my favorites to read because they're so powerful and beautiful, capturing you in the struggled lives of the people suffering and living with this illness they have. Every book I've read that is labeled as a "contemporary mental health book" has been one I've loved, like and enjoyed. I haven't ended up disliking any except <i>When We Collided by Emery Lord</i>, mostly because the main character, Viv, got on my nerves so many times to the point I wanted to throw her the shoe she threw at Jonah. My point is, reading mental health books can be something can read to heal them, inspire them, educate them, or merely entertain them. They can be a way for someone to escape because there's nowhere else to go. Although I'm giving this 3 stars, I still very much enjoyed it and would actually read it again, but there is a reason I'm giving it 3 and not 4 or 5. <b>A List of Cages is emotional and powerful and is not a book you just read for enjoyment.</b><br /><br /><i>A List of Cages</i> follows two foster brothers who were separated and haven't seen each other for 5 years after suddenly encountering each other in the school hallway. Adam is a senior with ADHD who has been assigned as a sort of assistant to the school psychologist for landing as the best elective. His job consists of taking Julian to the appointments he has been missing out on with the psychologist without asking much except tracking him down in school. Julian was first introduced to Adam when he was in Kindergarten because he was assigned to be Adam's buddy reader, later becoming his foster brother because his parents died but then being taken by his uncle, Russell. Ever since then, Julian has still been struggling with his learning disability, dyslexia, and has been living a life he is not able to change. When he bumps into Adam, all Julian thinks of is running away and avoiding him because he knows all the secrets he has been hiding from him, but little did he know that running into him would mean starting a new life.<br /><br /><b>A List of Cages is about finding new friendships and new people to rely on when you feel like everything is going downhill. It's about finding yourself and the people who love you. It's about the struggles you have to go through in life in order to start a new one very soon.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>It's strange how many ways there are to miss someone. You miss the things they did and who they were, but you also miss who you were to them. The way everything you said and did was beautiful or entertaining or important. How much you mattered.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br /><br /><b>Trigger/content warnings for</b> child abuse. It can be the reason one stops reading the book or continue reading the book, but it was so descriptive and emotional that all you want to do is put the book down because you don't know when it will end.<br /><br />When I first heard about this, I knew it had to do with mental health, such as ADHD since that is what Adam has, but I think the problem was that the mental illness was not really there. We don't see or hear much about Adam and his ADHD and how he copes with it. We were just told he stopped taking medicines or the things he had done to help himself. Truthfully, I don't even know if his friends knew about his ADHD because I sure as hell was not able to notice. The ADHD was rarely brought up. We didn't really see Adam struggling, we saw Julian struggling. I'm not saying the book should have been about Adam and his ADHD and I am not saying I wanted to see Adam struggle (I never want that in beautiful contemporary characters like these), all I'm saying is that I didn't get what I thought I would get. <br /><br />I don't have ADHD/ADD, but I have a friend who has ADHD and I remember how every day the nurse would come to our class and bring a small cup of water with a small capsule known as Albuterol. When I asked her what it was for, she told me what it was and what ADHD was for her. It saddened me to know how she struggles with learning and her education, but I know she didn't let her disability stop her. I also have another friend who has dyslexia but one thing that bothered me about him was that he would actually use it as an excuse as to WHY he wasn't able to learn like the rest. I understand it is more difficult and not easy to cope with, but using it for everything that had to do with your learning was getting really annoying to the point where I rolled my eyes everytime he said: "I have dyslexia." I mean, we only got Julian saying it once or twice but that was because he had to say he had it. My friend, on the other hand, would say he couldn't do something <i>because</i> he has dyslexia. I mean, it's 2018, you shouldn't let your mental health define you and stop you. I know it's different for everyone, but you don't see me telling my P.E. teacher I can't run because I have asthma. No, you see me telling my teacher I can run <i>because</i> I have asthma. <br /><br /><b>I truly felt bad for Julian in every way possible.</b> He was abused and hit and he couldn't do anything to stop it. His life was a living hell and he was not able to run or stop the abuse or tell anyone because he was scared, and it was easy to see where he was coming from. He felt like he lived in a nice home and felt like his uncle provided him enough, but because he felt like that, the way he was treated was totally normal for him. It was like he was used to being whipped, yelled at, pushed at, and even bullied. He was living a life no fourteen-year-old should be living. It's a life no one should be living. He had no friends and was made fun of because of what he did. He would read a book and a classmate would make fun of him because that classmates <i>little sibling</i> also read it, and he would get disgusting drawings on his book, making fun of him for his likes. Julian really deserved better. You can really get that feeling of wanting to take him out of the book and tell him everything will be fine.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Why is time like that? Why does it slow down in the places you don’t want it to, but it speeds away when you’re happy?</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br /><br />Friendship in this is something else that is important but was also missing. I admit, I really did enjoy the friendship between Julian and Adam. The two were foster brothers and were like real, biological brothers. <b>Their friendship was more than friendship and I think the way Robin Roe handled their reunion was so beautiful.</b> The book's message really is about friendship and how you can become so close to that person you were best friends 5 years ago. Julian was definitely missing a friend, and it really couldn't have been better than having his lost foster brother who is a senior. Julian was a freshman who was getting bullied, talked about behind his back, not cared for, not loved, not wanted, and having the care and love from Adam and his other senior friends were enough for Julian. I don't know what happened to the freshman who was bullying Julian, but I really hope they opened their eyes and realized that what they were doing was a shitty move. I mean, for fuck's sake even the teacher was a total bitch! You can't just act like a smartass with someone who has had a learning disability since he was small. Julian has proved himself that he can do something with the help and understanding of other people, but of the teachers, principal, and other students aren't going to lend him a hand, the poor boy is going to continue struggling. It's like that for everyone with a disability.<br /><br />Julian didn't have friends until he met Adam's friends. Adam's friends seemed to now know much about Adam as I thought they would. Adam's friend didn't like Julian at first because he's <i>creepy and shy</i>. Or well, mostly Charlie, but I could see where he was coming from. All Julian had was Russell, and it wasn't someone he wanted to have or someone he needed. It was just someone he had. That's all. <br /><br /><b>The other issue in this is understanding teachers and an understanding principal.</b> The teachers showed no sympathy towards Julian. They never bothered to ask how things were "at home" and how he was doing. They never seemed to care about his dyslexia. They never asked him if he preferred to work alone. They never let him choose anything on his own. There was no one who cared about Julian. The principal also showed no compassion towards him and didn't bother to care. The only person who truly cared, and showed it, was the school psychologist. I was honestly surprised because I didn't know high schools had a psychologist.<br /><br /><b>I know I've rambled a lot about disability issues in this book but that's because the issue here is that some people really do not understand what it is to live a life pretending you can do things right but in reality, you mess everything up because your brain is missing something that allows you to do things right.</b> Some people really think people with learning disabilities or mental illnesses in general use this illness as an excuse to get away with things but it's not because they want to, its because they have to or can't do it. It just is, and some people are so idiotic and full of bullshit that they end up hating you because you have "an advantage" when in reality, you wish you had a "normal brain" like theirs so you wouldn't be judged for it. Even in 2018, even in society now, people take mental health as a hoax. <b>It's ridiculous, sad, and embarrassing.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Because people heal a whole lot faster when they're with someone who loves them.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br /><br /><b>Now that I mention the psychologist again, I think she was a great addition to this novel.</b> She really did try to understand and help Julian and even though Julian didn't want her help, he ended up noticing she actually tried, unlike others, and I know that made him happy. Julian was a boy struggling to face his fears and, although this isn't a coming-of-age story, Julian is a boy who was growing from his past to finding out his future had so much waiting for him.<br /><br />The biggest problem I had with this was the ending. It felt so rushed and not enough details were given. It went from one scene to the other, and the author didn't tell us what happened after, it just dove into a whole different scene. Although I was met with a few problems here and there with this, the book was still enjoyable, heart-warming yet emotional, but it was not what I was expecting. It is sad, moving, touching, powerful yet inspiring, beautiful, and a book that has you remembering the characters and their struggles after you finish reading about them. <b>I really do recommend this for anyone looking for a quick yet emotionally driven sad contemporary.</b> <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>She said no one is evil, only unhappy, and unhappiness festers inside like sores.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12707175941376064898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1842997370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11982361508438623427">Honestly, don't touch me right now because MY EYES ARE A SWEATY MESS AND I DON'T EVEN CARE IF THAT SOUNDS EXTREMELY GROSS. I knew this book was going to be an emotional punch in the gut because <i>everyone</i> has been crying and raving about this. This book was heartbreaking from page one because my little Julian.<br/><br/>If you don't know already, I love sad, depressing, and heartbreaking books because I just love the suffering and pain sad books bring. But what I love most about "sad, depressing, and heartbr</span>
  <span id="freeText11982361508438623427" style="display:none">Honestly, don't touch me right now because MY EYES ARE A SWEATY MESS AND I DON'T EVEN CARE IF THAT SOUNDS EXTREMELY GROSS. I knew this book was going to be an emotional punch in the gut because <i>everyone</i> has been crying and raving about this. This book was heartbreaking from page one because my little Julian.<br /><br />If you don't know already, I love sad, depressing, and heartbreaking books because I just love the suffering and pain sad books bring. But what I love most about "sad, depressing, and heartbreaking" books is that stay with me for a long long time. I love how they aren't happy fairy tales, but the ugly and harsh truth about our world. This book is one of those kinds of books. And I strongly recommend you pick it up and read it. <br /><br /><i>! Spoilers ahead?? !</i><br /><br />TRIGGER WARNING: <b>Child abuse</b><br /><br /><i>A List of Cages</i> is about two teenagers, Julian and Adam who were once foster brothers, but then Julian is taken into custody by an uncle he never knew he had. Ever since, his life is a living fucking hell. Julian's beaten, whipped, isolated and terrified of everything. It was absolutely horrible and heartbreaking to read about this innocent fourteen year old boy being treated like this. <br /><br />Julian is one of the most sweetest, innocent, and forgiving characters ever. He's one of those people I would like to hug and feed vanilla ice cream with sprinkles on top to everyday !!!! Julian has been through so much a kid his age or anyone's age shouldn't have to go through AT ALL. And reading about his life made me cry so much because no one deserves what he went through. I loved him.<br /><br />Adam is such an amazing character as well. He was so friendly and lovable towards Julian. He's so caring, lovable, and kind towards everyone. (Except for Julian's asshole uncle which I totally understand.) Also, his ADHD was dealt with absolutely brilliantly. Though I enjoyed reading from his POV, I looked forward to Julians' POV's more. <br /><br />We seriously need more positive sibling relationships in YA books. The one in this book is one of the freaking best EVER. Like, I'm seriously crying over Adam and Julian's relationship. They love and care for each other so much and they are always there for each other. It's just so beautiful, my God.<br /><br /><b>Overall, if you're still having doubts about reading this, hit me up and I'll be there to throw this book in your face.</b></span>

<div id="review_1824143061" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1824143061" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1824143061?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5872506-larry-h?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1824143061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7114043250919118533">I'd rate this 4.5 stars.<br/><br/>This book is at times harrowing and heartbreaking, at times hopeful. But what adds to this book's power is the fact that its plot isn't fantasy, and there are children dealing with these issues every day.<br/><br/>Life changed for Julian five years ago when his beloved parents died. He lived with a foster family until a relative took him in. He misses his parents every day, and this loss truly encompasses him, because they understood him, they supported his creativity, and made lif</span>
  <span id="freeText7114043250919118533" style="display:none">I'd rate this 4.5 stars.<br /><br />This book is at times harrowing and heartbreaking, at times hopeful. But what adds to this book's power is the fact that its plot isn't fantasy, and there are children dealing with these issues every day.<br /><br />Life changed for Julian five years ago when his beloved parents died. He lived with a foster family until a relative took him in. He misses his parents every day, and this loss truly encompasses him, because they understood him, they supported his creativity, and made life fun.<br /><br />"It's strange how many ways there are to miss someone. You miss the things they did and who they were, but you also miss who you were to them. The way everything you said and did was beautiful or entertaining or important. How much you mattered."<br /><br />Now a high school freshman, life couldn't be further from fun. Julian has a number of learning disabilities, including dyslexia, which make school absolute hell for him, and his teachers don't care enough to find out what his problems are, they just berate him, fail him, and send him to the principal. His fellow students ridicule him as well. And he constantly feels as if he is living on eggshells at home, where one wrong step could spell disaster.<br /><br />One day, Julian is shocked to encounter Adam, who was once his foster brother. Adam, a high school senior assigned to help the school psychologist track down Julian for his appointments (which he always conveniently misses), is excited to see Julian again. He remembers many of the things Julian enjoyed when he was younger, and does everything he can to integrate Julian into his wide circle of friends, despite the difference in their ages, and despite Julian's efforts to try not to call attention to himself.<br /><br />Adam, who tries valiantly to keep his own ADHD in check (not always successfully), is dealing with his own issues, including a crush on a long-time friend, and his best friend Charlie's unhappiness. But he wants Julian to be a part of his life, and he wants to understand what is happening to him—why is he absent without warning for a few days, why is no one allowed over to his house, why would this relative that took Julian in all those years ago not pay for clothes that fit him?<br /><br />"He's only four years younger than me, but I feel so much older, or maybe he feels so much younger. I used to think struggle was what aged you, but if that were the case, Julian should've been a hundred years old. Now I wonder if the opposite is true. Maybe instead of accelerating your age, pain won't let you grow."<br /><br />Things come to a head when Adam starts suspecting things are worse for Julian than he lets on, and Julian tries desperately to keep his friend from finding out the truth. Adam's quest to rescue his friend could wind up seriously endangering both of their lives.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>A List of Cages</i>
</b> is a sad story that is all too commonplace. Julian is a tremendously special character whose hurt and pain reminded me a tiny bit of Jude's in <b>
  <i>A Little Life</i>
</b>, although the books are vastly different. I enjoyed Adam's character, too, as well as those of his friends and even his mother. I never felt that these kids were more erudite than they should be, which happens all too often in young adult novels.<br /><br />While the plot isn't necessarily surprising (perhaps we've sadly all become a little too familiar with instances like these), Robin Roe pulls you in to Julian and Adam's stories, makes you care, and makes you feel in the process. I could have done without the one melodramatic plot point, but beyond that, this story gripped me from start to finish. It's hard to read at times because it is so harrowing, but there is light at the end of the tunnel.<br /><br />I hope this book finds a wide audience because of its subject matter, but also because Roe's storytelling ability is so powerful. I'm glad I had the opportunity to read it.<br /><br />NetGalley and Disney-Hyperion provided me an advance copy of the book in exchange for an unbiased review. Thanks for making this available! <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7114043250919118533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2252850476" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2252850476" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2252850476?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2252850476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7142452269025011155"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565706030ra/27986802.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My heart.<br/><br/>While I understand this is not a perfect book, for me, it opened my eyes to the world of hard-hitting YA Contemporary writing, and for that, I will always be grateful.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512401637ra/24597426.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I knew that I would struggle trying to write an adequate review of this book. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550068928ra/27057438.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I just cannot express the way I feel about this one. <br/><br/>It was quite honestly one of, if not the most, moving story I have ever read. Amazingly well done and I feel it should be required reading.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548532925ra/26974448.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/>The story follows two characters, Julian and Adam. <br/><br/>Ju</span>
  <span id="freeText7142452269025011155" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565706030ra/27986802.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My heart.<br><br>While I understand this is not a perfect book, for me, it opened my eyes to the world of hard-hitting YA Contemporary writing, and for that, I will always be grateful.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512401637ra/24597426.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I knew that I would struggle trying to write an adequate review of this book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550068928ra/27057438.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just cannot express the way I feel about this one. <br><br>It was quite honestly one of, if not the most, moving story I have ever read. Amazingly well done and I feel it should be required reading.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548532925ra/26974448.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>The story follows two characters, Julian and Adam. <br><br>Julian, the younger of the two, lost his parents to an accident when he was just a child. Due to a lack of any other immediate family, young Julian, is forced into 'the system'. <br><br>Adam's Mother, a social worker, ends up taking him in as a foster child and thus, the boys essentially become brothers for a time. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581952287ra/28977590.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unexpectedly, a distant relation (by marriage) of Julian's comes forward and claims him and he moves into a new home and a new life, having no further contact with Adam until high school. This is where our story picks up.<br><br>These characters are so well drawn. Julian, so sweet, innocent and trapped in his loss. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550068928ra/27057436.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Adam, fun, popular and extremely caring brings humor and understanding to the narrative.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550068928ra/27057437.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I love the relationship between the two boys and how it evolves over the course of the book. While annotating, I tabbed so many sections, passages and sentences as there are a lot of very important ideas and issued tackled. <br><br>I feel like Robin Roe's real life experiences working with 'at-risk' teens helped add to the realistic feel of this novel. <b>This will be a hard one to forget.</b> <br><br>Nothing short of heartbreaking.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550068928ra/27057439.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly, I was shattered after reading this but also felt filled with love and hope. I ended up feeling such a strong connections to these boys; I really became attached in a way I don't think I have experienced before. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550068928ra/27057435.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book teaches a <b>message of kindness and empathy</b>. Be kind to all, as you can never truly know what someone else is going through; what someone's reality is and your kindness may be the only they receive that day. Seriously. I know that sounds lame but I honestly believe that. <br><br>I will be recommending this book to everyone in the world from this day forward. I caution readers that you shouldn't expect a light fluffy read here. There are definitely moments of humor, Adam's character in particular is very funny, but this book deals with <u>very serious issues of abuse, both mental and physical, death, grief, loss, self worth and self preservation</u>. <br><br>Absolutely brilliant!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475755533ra/20762056.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="7142452269025011155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14112434558547401826" style="display:none">I’m numb. Mainly due to the part that I almost had to numb my feelings because of the injustice, the anger and the trauma that all takes part in this story. That love and understanding and stories are what carry pain away and allow you to see light. </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=contemporaries">contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t">finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1825700065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15286853079523079055"><b>2.5 Stars </b> <br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> “Hate ricochets, but kindness does too.” </blockquote>
</i> <br/><br/>This is a book that says some beautiful, important things, but uses an exploitive, painful abuse storyline to do so. <br/><br/>…okay. Bear with me. I know that’s a <i>big</i> statement, and I know the majority disagrees with me. But the whole time I read this… I just felt unsettled? The overwhelming focus is on the <b>physical manifestations of abuse</b> and very little on any healing? Sure, the narrative mentions healing, but the plot is just one horrible, horr</span>
  <span id="freeText15286853079523079055" style="display:none"><b>2.5 Stars </b> <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “Hate ricochets, but kindness does too.” </blockquote>
</i> <br /><br />This is a book that says some beautiful, important things, but uses an exploitive, painful abuse storyline to do so. <br /><br />…okay. Bear with me. I know that’s a <i>big</i> statement, and I know the majority disagrees with me. But the whole time I read this… I just felt unsettled? The overwhelming focus is on the <b>physical manifestations of abuse</b> and very little on any healing? Sure, the narrative mentions healing, but the plot is just one horrible, horrible abuse after another, and as soon as the abuse stops there’s just a rushed-haphazard ending—like there was nothing left to resolve or discuss? <br /><br />This also felt apparent in the way <b>every single adult was a horrible archetype.</b> Whether it was Julian’s monster of an uncle, numerous dimwitted and mean school teachers or Adam’s nice, but completely oblivious mother… none of the adults were helpful. It continued to amp up the drama of the situation and create another kids-don’t-trust-adults-or-ask-for-help story. <br /><br />It’s not that this book was poorly written… <i>it wasn’t!</i> It features <b>some great ADHD representation in a likeable, extroverted narrator</b> as well as Julian-the-precious-cinnamon-roll. I loved that the focus was on friendship/brotherhood, compared to the ever-popular romance. The romance that was present was cute, and featured a brief, but important discussion of consent and sex positivity. <br /><br /><b>Overall:</b><br />I couldn’t move past the main, brutal storyline and how it used an abuse victim just for the shock factor.<br /> Maybe it's just me. Maybe I just never connected with the story. Maybe I missed something. Maybe I'm dead inside.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15286853079523079055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17065991-ikram?shelf=smells-like-pain">smells-like-pain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17065991-ikram?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17065991-ikram?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1805822699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3832708405661036465"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479578617i/21209368.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Out today! <br/><br/>(I received a free arc from Netgally in exchange for an honest review. This book comes out in January 2017.)<br/><br/><b>"I used to think that if I concentrated, I could make myself disappear. I don't believe that anymore, but sometimes I still have to try."</b><br/><br/>Trigger warning: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Child abuse.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>Holy guacamole. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456464722ra/18237193.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I think I've just been eaten by a giant blob of feels. This was one of easiest five stars I've given so far this year. This book is definitely the next big thing. Li</span>
  <span id="freeText3832708405661036465" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479578617i/21209368.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Out today! <br><br>(I received a free arc from Netgally in exchange for an honest review. This book comes out in January 2017.)<br><br><b>"I used to think that if I concentrated, I could make myself disappear. I don't believe that anymore, but sometimes I still have to try."</b><br><br>Trigger warning: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Child abuse.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Holy guacamole. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456464722ra/18237193.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think I've just been eaten by a giant blob of feels. This was one of easiest five stars I've given so far this year. This book is definitely the next big thing. Like the next TFIOS or The Perks of Being a Wallflower. <br><br><u>This is a list of what I liked about this book:</u> (See what I did there? A list? Anyone? Okay.) <br><br>➨ <b> Mental Health: </b> I'm not sure why but I have a soft spot for books that deal with mental Health issues. Not all illnesses are visible after all, but it's important to keep in mind that mental illnesses are just as severe as physical ones. This book deals with a main character that suffers from ADHD which was extremely interesting since I've never read any book that mentioned this condition before. <br><br>➨ <b> The writing Style: </b> I found myself rereading some sentences over and over again just because they were written in such a beautiful way you can't help but want to memorise them. <br><blockquote>"It's strange how many ways there are to miss someone. You miss the things they did and who they were, but you also miss who you were with them. The way everything you said and did was beautiful or entertaining or important. How much you mattered."</blockquote><br>➨<b> Julian: </b> Julian is one of those characters you just want to hug. For the rest of your life. <br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479597259ra/21211785.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>He's been through so much but he kept his soul intact. One of the sweetest characters I've ever read about. <br><br>➨<b> The tears! </b> Usually, it's a good sign when a book succeeds at making me cry so bonus points for you Robin Roe! <br><br>Overall, a very powerful read. I loved every page of this book and I would highly recommended to pretty much everyone. <br><br>Thanks for reading. Please share your thoughts. <br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1845800049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845800049" />
    <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic"><img alt="Irena BookDustMagic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362943196p2/17737927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1845800049?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irena BookDustMagic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irena BookDustMagic" href="/user/show/17737927-irena-bookdustmagic">Irena BookDustMagic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845800049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11046325024935421794">A List of Cages is not a book that grabs your attention immediately.<br/>At least, it was not in my case.<br/>I saw it’s cover on Netgalley, but didn’t pay much attention to it until I got an invitation to review it.<br/>That invitation made me read what this story is actually about, and, since it sounded interesting and like something that could possibly make me learn something new, I decided to give it a try.<br/>I am so glad I did! <b>This book ended up as one of the best books I read in 2016, because of the powerf</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11046325024935421794" style="display:none">A List of Cages is not a book that grabs your attention immediately.<br />At least, it was not in my case.<br />I saw it’s cover on Netgalley, but didn’t pay much attention to it until I got an invitation to review it.<br />That invitation made me read what this story is actually about, and, since it sounded interesting and like something that could possibly make me learn something new, I decided to give it a try.<br />I am so glad I did! <b>This book ended up as one of the best books I read in 2016, because of the powerful message it brings.</b><br /><br />The story centres around two boys: <b>Adam</b> and <b>Julian. It is told in first person, from both boys’ POV.</b><br /><br />I loved how <b>author managed for both voices to sound differently,</b> which is very important for me when it comes to alternating perspectives.<br />I enjoyed reading both point of views, but I have to admit that <b>Adam’s was more enjoyable for me, because Julien’s was sometimes too hard to read </b>(emotinally).<br /><br />That’s why I question whether the word “enjoyed” is the right one to use.<b> This book was great, even perfect at some point, but it was also very, very hard at times.</b><br />Some situations in this story were <b>emotinally draining.</b><br />Robin Roe is not afraid to tell the story in realistic way. There’s no sugarcoating.<br /><b>The violence is described in a way that it is not too descriptive, but shows you enough to make your eyes tear up.</b><br /><br />This is a work of fiction, but I honestly believe that similar cases to Julien’s are happening right now in the world we live in (I still remember one episode of Oprah Show that I watched when I was a kid, with three brothers with similar fate as Julien’s).<br />Therefore, A List of Cages is so important! I think people of all ages should read it, and after they do, they should talk about it, talk about what happened in this story and make others read it too.<br /><br />This book tells us how important it is to find our voice and talk. And for those who can’t, we have to help them find their voices, encourage them in a way we can, and never stop talking.<br />There are so many awful things going on in the world right now, and raising our voices is one way we can at least try to make things better.<br /><br />Although A List of Cages is a novel that talks about serious topic, it also shows life of teenagers in a realistic way.<br />There are funny scenes and everyday life moments.<br />Parties, chrushes and bonding also found their places on pages.<br />Because of that aspect, <b>this novel reminded me of The Perks of Being a Wallflower (the movie,</b> I still haven’t read the book. Oh, and in case you didn’t know, The Perks of Being a Wallflower is my all-time favorite movie. Ever!).<br /><br /><b>Robin Roe did an amazing job when it comes to characterization.</b><br />Her focus was not only on Adam and Julien who are “stars” of the story, but she also created side characters who weren’t only interesting, but also went through development as well.<br /><b>My favorite character was Charlie.</b> I loved his story and enjoyed reading about him.<br /><br /><b>The writing style is really good.<br />Once you start reading, it’s hard to stop, and it reads quickly.</b><br />If my Nook didn’t chrash in the middle of reading, I would probably finish it even faster then I did.<br /><br />Overall, <b>A List of Cages is a book that should find itself on everyone’s tbr lists.</b><br />I know that there’s still no book that everyone likes, but in this case,<b> I really think that many people should at least give it a try.</b><br /><br /><i>Note: I got this book via Netgalley in an exchange for an honest review. Thank you Disney-hyperion. </i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Read this and more reviews on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bookdustmagic.com">https://bookdustmagic.com</a> </i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11046325024935421794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1798580084?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2016</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1798580084" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11156135891258284056"><b>
  <i>Warning:</i>
</b> Only read this book if you’re prepared for intense feelings of pain, anguish, and some awesomesauce friendship/brotherhood. <br/><br/>From the reviews I’ve read from my friends, I knew this book would be heartbreaking, but I didn’t expect it to be the rip-your-heart-out-of-your-chest-and-stomp-on-it-until-it-desingrates type of heartbreak. <br/><br/>. . . turns out it was.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493228597i/22594456.jpg' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The chapters switch alternatively between Julian ((my baby))’s perspective and Adam ((my baby)’s perspective. Julian needs to be pro</span>
  <span id="freeText11156135891258284056" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Warning:</i>
</b> Only read this book if you’re prepared for intense feelings of pain, anguish, and some awesomesauce friendship/brotherhood. <br><br>From the reviews I’ve read from my friends, I knew this book would be heartbreaking, but I didn’t expect it to be the rip-your-heart-out-of-your-chest-and-stomp-on-it-until-it-desingrates type of heartbreak. <br><br>. . . turns out it was.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493228597i/22594456.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The chapters switch alternatively between Julian ((my baby))’s perspective and Adam ((my baby)’s perspective. Julian needs to be protected at all costs and everyone needs an Adam Blake in their life. Honestly, he’s literally the most sweetest, caring, older-brother-figure, my heart is tearing up again. <br><br>The writing is honestly SO easy to get into and the fact that the chapters are hella short make the pace steady and attention grabbing. <br><br>There are many things in this book that will make you feel incredibly uneasy ((again, protect baby Julian)) but I think that just adds more to the pain of the book. <br><br>Lots of tears will be shed, did i mention that???? :)))))<br><br>Also, the mental health ((regarding Adam)) was dealt with BRILLIANTLY. Honestly, it was objective and honest and not in any way degrading. <br><br>I genuinely love this book. <br><br>Okay, if I start talking about anything else, I’m gonna end up spewing my feels and exposing MASSIVE **spoilers** and I’d rather not do that but just know that tears await you when you pick up this book. <br><br><i> “It's strange how many ways there are to miss someone. You miss the things they did and who they were, but you also miss who you were to them. The way everything you said and did was beautiful or entertaining or important. How much you mattered”</i><br><br>5 stars!!!<br><br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br><i> buddy reading with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069" rel="nofollow noopener">the ditcher™</a> </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11156135891258284056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1882960376" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1882960376" />
    <a title="Sara (sarawithoutanH)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7397330-sara-sarawithoutanh"><img alt="Sara (sarawithoutanH)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545592752p2/7397330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1882960376?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara (sarawithoutanH)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara (sarawithoutanH)" href="/user/show/7397330-sara-sarawithoutanh">Sara (sarawithoutanH)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7397330-sara-sarawithoutanh?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1882960376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13867371450955938710">First and foremost, I loved the message of this book. It’s not often that you find a YA book that primarily highlights the meaning of friendship and kindness. It was refreshing to read a book that didn’t focus on romance. I absolutely loved Julian. He was an adorable cinnamon roll. The second half of this book is absolutely heartbreaking and I just wanted to give Julian a big hug. <br/><br/>Julian: <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484679383ra/21741507.gif' width='160' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My main critique with this book is the writing style. While there were some very meaningful and quotable exc</span>
  <span id="freeText13867371450955938710" style="display:none">First and foremost, I loved the message of this book. It’s not often that you find a YA book that primarily highlights the meaning of friendship and kindness. It was refreshing to read a book that didn’t focus on romance. I absolutely loved Julian. He was an adorable cinnamon roll. The second half of this book is absolutely heartbreaking and I just wanted to give Julian a big hug. <br><br>Julian: <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484679383ra/21741507.gif" width="160" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My main critique with this book is the writing style. While there were some very meaningful and quotable excerpts, overall I thought the writing quality was inconsistent. It had a bit of a middle grade vibe and I just tend to be someone who doesn’t enjoy that. I thought the two main characters were developed, but the side characters lacked depth and felt like rough sketches of people. For some reason almost every single adult character was extremely terrible and unhelpful to the main characters. While I do understand that not every adult has the ability to deal with troubled kids, it felt a bit unrealistic that almost every teacher or police officer that they encountered would be *that* mean. <br><br>But with those criticisms aside, I think the strength of this book is its message. I think this is an important book for younger readers. I think I would have really enjoyed it when I was in high school. Julian and Adam’s narrative is one that I think can have a positive impact on readers. I think Roe covers mental health and child abuse in a very important way. It’s a very sweet and special read. <br><br><b>I was sent an ARC of this book by Disney Hyperion in exchange for an honest review.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13867371450955938710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
